<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="module-content">Module content<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#module-content" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="module-units">Module Units:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#module-units" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p> Concepts and principles in facilitative supervision
 Mentorship, Coaching and Counseling</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-c183da2b.jpeg" alt="img-4.jpeg"></p>
<p>Unit 1: Concepts and principles in facilitative supervision</p>
<p>unit time: 20hrs</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-166036ab.jpeg" alt="img-5.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-a9023ce4.jpeg" alt="img-6.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="definition-of-terms-concepts">Definition of terms &amp; concepts<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition-of-terms-concepts" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>A. Supervision: refers to an act by which any person inspects the work of other people, i.e., whether they are working properly or not</p>
<p>B. Also refers to the direct &amp; immediate guidance &amp; control of subordinates in the performance of their tasks</p>
<p>&gt; Its direction, guidance &amp; control of working force with a view to see:
&gt; (i) that they are working according to plan &amp;,
&gt; (ii) are observing &amp; adhering to time schedules.</p>
<p>B. Supervisors: those having authority to exercise independent judgment in hiring, discharging, disciplining, rewarding &amp; taking other actions of a similar nature with respect to employees'</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-bb59e182.jpeg" alt="img-7.jpeg"></p>
<p>5</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="definitions-cont-d">Definitions ... (Cont'd)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definitions-cont-d" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Facilitative supervision: a process of guiding, monitoring &amp; coaching workers to promote compliance with standards of practice &amp; assure the delivery of quality care services.
 Supervisory process permits supervisors &amp; supervisees the opportunity to work as a team to meet common goals and objectives
 Also known as supportive supervision</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-9b566698.jpeg" alt="img-8.jpeg"></p>
<p>6</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="definitions-cont-d">DEFINITIONS CONT'D<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definitions-cont-d" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> supervision is concerned with three main functions of management,</p>
<p>A. Directing,
B. Guiding and,
C. Controlling
&gt; F.S is a best practice for CHW supervision in international settings</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-293fa2f1.jpeg" alt="img-9.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="traditional-supervision">TRADITIONAL SUPERVISION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#traditional-supervision" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> A superficial/Shallow process that only looks at the face value of the problem &amp; not the root cause  no set standards.
 It is often punitive, fault-finding does not offer solutions.
 Focuses on individuals rather than processes
 Does not endeavor to strengthen systems and processes that may cause disconnect between current outputs of health care to the expected standards</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-293fa2f1.jpeg" alt="img-10.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="aa4406d0">Traditional supervision (contd)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aa4406d0" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Emphasizes the past rather than the future.
 Its not continuous but its rather intermittent
 usually creates resentment, suspicion, and disintegration between team members rather than focusing on strengthening team work for quality service delivery.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-293fa2f1.jpeg" alt="img-11.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="facilitative-supervision-also-includes">Facilitative supervision also includes...<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#facilitative-supervision-also-includes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Collaborative reviews,</li>
<li>Observations,</li>
<li>Monitoring - identifies problems and opportunities,</li>
<li>Coordination - support community health service providers in service delivery.</li>
<li>Constructive feedback - emphasizing building confidence and self-esteem</li>
<li>Active participation,</li>
<li>Problem-solving, and</li>
<li>Training and education</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-293fa2f1.jpeg" alt="img-12.jpeg"></p>
<p>10</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="facilitative-supervision-emphasis">FACILITATIVE SUPERVISION EMPHASIS:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#facilitative-supervision-emphasis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Mentoring
 Joint problem solving
 2-way communication between supervisor
 Those being supervised</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-9ed4766b.jpeg" alt="img-13.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="benefits-of-facilitative-supervision">BENEFITS OF FACILITATIVE SUPERVISION:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#benefits-of-facilitative-supervision" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Fewer routine, low-level problems to solve
 Less supervision work with less technical assistance since workers know how to do it
 Gaining reputation as a leader, an effective supervisor, &amp; an enabler
 Always welcome at sites - you help staff solve their problems, rather than criticize them for their faults</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-b9f287a4.jpeg" alt="img-14.jpeg"></p>
<p>12</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="benefits-cont-d">Benefits (cont'd)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#benefits-cont-d" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Satisfaction of working as a team member, watching staff learn and grow and watching quality improve
 More fulfilling jobs as staff's motivation &amp; commitment increase
 Staff will openly share problems</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-058c7527.jpeg" alt="img-15.jpeg"></p>
<p>13</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="principles-of-supervision">Principles of supervision<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-of-supervision" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Right intensity: Lesser the weight of supervision higher the output. So a supervisor must be given optimum work.</p>
<p> Personal interest: supervisors should take personal interest in the welfare of the workers under them. Consultations: A good supervisor must consult people under them. They can afford opportunities for free and frank discussion of issues and problems.</p>
<p> Loyalty: they must exhibit their loyalty to the subordinates by safeguarding their interests. They should not offend the dignity of workers</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-4bf378be.jpeg" alt="img-16.jpeg"></p>
<p>14</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="principles-of-supervision-cont-d">Principles of supervision (cont'd)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-of-supervision-cont-d" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Informal assessment: Informal appraisal of the performance of the subordinates and pointing out their shortcomings with a view to improve.</p>
<p> Broader interest: Supervisors are expected to take interest in management functions like planning, organizing, directing and controlling.</p>
<p> Work climate: They can create better work climate for successful achievements. Any strain in work climate will spoil the whole organization.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-b9f287a4.jpeg" alt="img-17.jpeg"></p>
<p>15</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="why-is-f-s-different-from-t-s">Why is F.S different from t.s<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#why-is-f-s-different-from-t-s" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Focuses on helping staff solve problems through using quality-improvement tools  T.S Does not
 Focuses on processes rather than on individuals - T.S Does not
 Assists staff in planning for future quality-improvement goals - T.S Does not
 Is continuous and builds on past gains while setting higher quality-improvement goals - T.S is not</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-4bf378be.jpeg" alt="img-18.jpeg"></p>
<p>16</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="a-good-facilitative-supervisor-qualities">A good facilitative supervisor... (Qualities)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-good-facilitative-supervisor-qualities" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Good listener
 More knowledgeable in technical issues than the community health service providers (It is ok for the supervisor not to know everything, but they can enquire)
 Resourceful (problem-solving skills) e.g. being able to make things happen when confronted by obstacles.
 Good communication skills
 Supportive
 Respectful
 Acts as a role model
 Has good mentorship and coaching skills</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-b9f287a4.jpeg" alt="img-19.jpeg"></p>
<p>17</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="functions-of-supervision">FUNCTIONS OF SUPERVISION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#functions-of-supervision" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Educative (formative)  professional development of the supervisee
 Supportive (restorative)  welfare of the supervisee
 Administrative (normative)quality assurance, managing supplies, scheduling appointments, filing information, answering phone calls etc</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-9b566698.jpeg" alt="img-20.jpeg"></p>
<p>18</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="assignment">ASSIGNMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assignment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Relationship building is one of the tasks of supportive supervision. Discuss this relationship between the supervisor and the community health service provider.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-b9f287a4.jpeg" alt="img-21.jpeg"></p>
<p>19</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="supervision-tasks">SUPERVISION TASKS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#supervision-tasks" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Monitoring  the professional &amp; ethical aspects of supervision
 Support  deals with personal issues as they emerge from work
 Teaching  e.g., modeling &amp; other methods such as role playing (recedes as experience is gained)
 Evaluation  seasonally assessing the performance of the staff.
 Consultation  to know what's happening with clients.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-8bb0588a.jpeg" alt="img-22.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="supervision-tasks">Supervision Tasks<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#supervision-tasks" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="a468c31c"><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo></mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\rightarrow</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.3669em;"></span><span class="mrel"></span></span></span></span></span>  Administration<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a468c31c" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Help solve logistical challenges</p>
<ul>
<li>Conduct spot-checks to ensure CHVs/CHOs are working as per established standards
Accompany individual CHVs on household visits to assess performance.</li>
<li>Improve cooperation by acting as a link between CHVs and the tier one facilities</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-293fa2f1.jpeg" alt="img-23.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="supervision-tasks-administration-cont-d">Supervision tasks (administration cont'd)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#supervision-tasks-administration-cont-d" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Provide mentorship to CHVs</li>
<li>Discuss performance and provide constructive feedback on one-on-one with the CHVs</li>
<li>Ensure quality assurance in service delivery</li>
<li>Compile reports</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-2c9e338f.jpeg" alt="img-24.jpeg"></p>
<p>22</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="challenges-to-supervision">Challenges to supervision<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#challenges-to-supervision" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Travel expense and logistics
 Supervisors are really not supervisors
 Supervisors do not have appropriate tools and support to conduct supervision
 Supervision is not a priority
 Supervisors dont understand the CHWs role or the context in which they operate
 Gender issues complicate the supervisory process because often supervisors are men and CHWs are women</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-a9e9a3fb.jpeg" alt="img-25.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="professional-issues-in-supervision">Professional issues in Supervision<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#professional-issues-in-supervision" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Competency  provide services for which you are qualified by training and experience
 Minimum amount of supervisor-supervisee contact--for example, no of hours per week, total number of hours
 Number of supervisees allowed
 Format of supervision  for example, individual vs. group, face-to-face vs. phone or e-mail, etc.
 Documentation of supervisory activities,</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-8bb0588a.jpeg" alt="img-26.jpeg"></p>
<p>24</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="ethical-issues-in-supervision">Ethical issues in supervision<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ethical-issues-in-supervision" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Autonomy  freedom of choice and responsibility of ones behaviour,
 Beneficence: Client/supervisee welfare, doing what is right
 Non-maleficence  do not harm staff
 Justice-treat all staff equally
 Confidentiality  information obtained should not be shared out</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-9ed4766b.jpeg" alt="img-27.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="ethical-issues-cont-d">Ethical issues (cont'd)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ethical-issues-cont-d" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Moral and legal standards, - e.g., Fidelity (loyalty, faithfulness, promise-keeping)
 Public statement  ensure that supervisees represent themselves correctly to the public
 Professional relationships- facilitate further professional development for the supervisees</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-2c9e338f.jpeg" alt="img-28.jpeg"></p>
<p>26</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="supervisory-visits">Supervisory visits<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#supervisory-visits" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> An activity conducted by supervisors to supervisees to check the progress of work discuss way forward and solve any challenges or conflicts that may exist.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-afc7fe0d.jpeg" alt="img-29.jpeg"></p>
<p>27</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="methods-used-during-supervisory-visits">Methods used during supervisory visits<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#methods-used-during-supervisory-visits" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Observation</li>
<li>Dialogue/discussion</li>
<li>Review of records</li>
<li>Exit interviews</li>
<li>Community interviews</li>
<li>Good supervision involves interaction, is supportive, not punitive!</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-2c9e338f.jpeg" alt="img-30.jpeg"></p>
<p>28</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="frequency-of-supervisory-visits">Frequency of supervisory visits<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#frequency-of-supervisory-visits" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Frequently enough to provide needed support
 Monthly to health facilities and community level
 Quarterly to sub-counties
 Every six months to Regional/Provincial level</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-293fa2f1.jpeg" alt="img-31.jpeg"></p>
<p>29</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="preparing-for-a-supervisory-visit">Preparing for a supervisory visit<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preparing-for-a-supervisory-visit" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Review past performance at the CU
 Find out about follow-up actions
 Collect appropriate checklists and recording forms
 Prepare to inform staff at the CU of any updates, plans
 Collect supplies, equipment, and/or materials that can be delivered
 Collect materials to take so that you will be prepared for problem solving
 Confirm logistic arrangements</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-293fa2f1.jpeg" alt="img-32.jpeg"></p>

AP MUTUA
117</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="steps-to-conduct-a-supervisory-visit">Steps to conduct a supervisory visit<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#steps-to-conduct-a-supervisory-visit" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Private interview with the person in-charge
 A review and assessment of current practices, procedures, logistics (walk about)
 A technical assessment of the performance of the health workers and the health services
 A discussion of perceptions of services and activities with caregivers
 Feedback of results
 An opportunity for health workers to ask questions
 Problem solving
 Plan for next steps.
 Action after the visit</p>
<p>31
M.P. MUTUA</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="techniques-for-giving-feedback">Techniques for giving feedback<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#techniques-for-giving-feedback" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Comments task oriented
 Feedback should be prompt
 Motivating
 Action-oriented
 Constructive</p>

M.P. MUTUA</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="how-to-conduct-a-problem-solving-discussion">How to conduct a problem-solving discussion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-to-conduct-a-problem-solving-discussion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Identify the likely cause (causes) of the problem
 Responsibility of the task clearly assigned?
 CHV/CHOs lack necessary knowledge and skills?
 CHV/CHOs lack motivation?
 Are there obstacles (time, authority, funds, supplies, etc.)
 Define one or more feasible solutions</p>

M.P. MUTUA</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="key-supervisory-tasks-motivate-provide-feedback">Key supervisory tasks: Motivate &amp; Provide feedback<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#key-supervisory-tasks-motivate-provide-feedback" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Resolve performance problems
 Blend employee goals with work requirements
 Improve communications and keep employees informed
 Responsibility for employee training and skills development</p>
<p>34</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="role-play-conduct-supervisory-visit-give-feedback-and-solve-problems">Role Play: Conduct supervisory visit, give feedback and solve problems<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#role-play-conduct-supervisory-visit-give-feedback-and-solve-problems" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>For this part of the exercise, you will practice conducting a supervisory visit, and giving feedback. One person will play the role of the supervisor and one will play the role of a health worker at a level 2 health facility. (Case study)</p>
<p>Health Centre setting:
 2 health workers attending to a patient in the OPD
 Supervisor comes in unannounced (walks in hands inside pocket)
 Asks for all staff member to assemble (stands akimbo)
 Takes roll call (identifies absentees)
 Ask staff members if they know his position
 Introduces himself
 Scribbles down some few notes
 He tells the staff members present, all absentees will hear from the Headquarters very soon He departs, fuming (without any guidance)</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-9b566698.jpeg" alt="img-33.jpeg"></p>

<p>a. Mentorship</p>
<p>38</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="what-is-it">What is it?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-is-it" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Mentoring: a process of deploying experienced individuals to provide guidance and advice that will help to develop the careers of mentees allocated to them.</p>
<p> Mentoring is the transfer and exchange of information between a mentor and a mentee as they develop a long-term relationship</p>
<p> Mentee: A person who takes charge of their own development and sees real value in learning from others (Goodman, 2004)</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-233f8270.jpeg" alt="img-38.jpeg"></p>
<p>39</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mentoring-relationship">Mentoring Relationship<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mentoring-relationship" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> A rship between two or more people, (whether formalized or not) with a specific purpose.
 The rship is reciprocal &amp; both parties benefit, albeit in different ways.
 The mentor-mentee rship is dynamic with different stages or phases.
 Each mentor-mentee relationship is unique.
 This rship transcends duty &amp; obligation &amp; often involves coaching, networking, sponsoring &amp; career counselling". (Meyer, M 2006).</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-a9e9a3fb.jpeg" alt="img-39.jpeg"></p>
<p>40</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="types-of-mentoring-relationships">Types of mentoring Relationships<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-mentoring-relationships" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Traditional One-on-one Mentoring  A mentee &amp; mentor are matched, either through a program or on their own. Mentee-mentor partners participate in a mentoring relationship with structure and timeframe of their making or as established by a formal mentoring program.</li>
<li>Distance Mentoring  the two parties (or group) are in different locations. Sometimes called virtual/E mentoring.</li>
<li>Group Mentoring  A single mentor is matched with <del>cohort</del> of mentees. Initial program structure is provided while allowing mentor to direct progress, pace and activities.</li>
</ul>
<p>41</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mentees-want-different-things">Mentees Want Different Things<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mentees-want-different-things" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Help
 Guidance
 Insights
 To be challenged
 To learn the secrets
 Brainstorming partner
 Oral presentation skills</p>
<p> Introductions to others
 Someone to help identify opportunities to present
 Grant writing skills
 Collaboration skills
 To be directed</p>
<p>M.P. MUTUA</p>
<p>42</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="questions-for-mentees">Questions for Mentees<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#questions-for-mentees" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> What do you want out of a mentoring relationship?
 What goals have you set for yourself?</p>
<ul>
<li>Long term? Short term? Where do you want to focus now?
 How do you learn best?
 How do you like to be challenged?
 How frequently do you want to meet?</li>
<li>What happens if one of us needs to cancel? If one of us does not show up for an appointment?
 What norms do we have? Rules?
 Etc...?</li>
</ul>
<p>43
M.P. MUTUA</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mentoring-plan">Mentoring Plan<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mentoring-plan" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Develop a mentoring plan based on your questions and the discussion about how you will work together</p>
<p> Plan can include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Setting professional goals</li>
<li>How you will achieve the goals</li>
<li>Role of the mentor in your career development</li>
<li>What you expect from mentor</li>
</ul>
<p>44
LIP MUTUA</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="schedule-meetings-when">Schedule Meetings When:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#schedule-meetings-when" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> You Can Listen Actively
 Pay Attention</p>
<ul>
<li>Look at the person you are talking to and wipe all other thoughts out of your mind
 Show That You're Listening</li>
<li>Nod, smile, uh-huh, etc...
 Check-in to be sure you are understanding</li>
<li>Paraphrase, summarize what theyve told you, ask clarifying questions
 Do not Judge</li>
<li>Dont interrupt before they finish their thought
 Respond Appropriately</li>
<li>Be open and honest, demonstrate respect</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="objectives-of-the-mentoring-rship">Objectives of the Mentoring Rship<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives-of-the-mentoring-rship" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> To drive a high performance organization
 To promote skills and knowledge transfer
 To enhance leadership capabilities
 To embed transformation which encourages a diverse workforce
 To reinforce learning and development
 Driving organization change within Public Finance Management</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-b9f287a4.jpeg" alt="img-40.jpeg"></p>
<p>46</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="characteristics-of-a-mentoring-rship">Characteristics of a mentoring rship<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics-of-a-mentoring-rship" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Dynamic - growth &amp; knowledge transfer.
 Reciprocal relationship
 Takes place within the work environment.
 Mentor is the wise career incumbent.
 Mentor is focused on helping the mentee (Less experienced) develop his or her potential.
 Mentor is not the direct supervisor of the mentee, but a third party such as a manager in a different dept.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-afc7fe0d.jpeg" alt="img-41.jpeg"></p>
<p>47</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="characteristics-cont-d">Characteristics ... (cont'd)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics-cont-d" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> The mentee is developed in some specified capacity (in other words there must be a clear purpose and focus for development through mentoring).</p>
<p> Mentoring is not about being sponsored for promotion</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-85581b85.jpeg" alt="img-42.jpeg"></p>
<p>48</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-role-of-the-mentor">The role of the mentor<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-role-of-the-mentor" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> To provide career development behaviors such as coaching
 To provide challenging assignments
 To foster the mentees visibility.
 To provide psychosocial support such as counseling, support and role modelling</p>
<p>NB: The role of the mentor is not merely to provide guidance &amp; advice on how to accomplish certain tasks skillfully.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-6095fd25.jpeg" alt="img-43.jpeg"></p>
<p>49</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="role-of-the-mentee">Role of the mentee<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#role-of-the-mentee" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> To assume responsibility for their own growth and to see feedback from the mentor as an opportunity to grow and improve their skills.</p>
<p> For mentoring to work the mentor co-creates a learning partnership with a mentee.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-2c9e338f.jpeg" alt="img-44.jpeg"></p>
<p>50</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mentorship-benefits-to-different-parties">Mentorship benefits to different parties<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mentorship-benefits-to-different-parties" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>The Mentors</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li> Get more opportunities to apply leadership skills</li>

The Organization<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-the-organization" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="qualities-of-a-good-mentor">Qualities of a Good Mentor?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#qualities-of-a-good-mentor" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Posses relevant expertise or knowledge.
 Enthusiasm for sharing that expertise.
 A respectful attitude.
 Eagerness to invest in others.
 The ability to give honest and direct feedback
 Reflective listening and empathy.
 Willingness to be a sponsor.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-058c7527.jpeg" alt="img-45.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mentorship-skills-characteristics-of-mentors-in-tier-ones-mentees-coachees-need-to">Mentorship skills &amp; characteristics of mentors in tier ones (Mentees/coachees need to:)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mentorship-skills-characteristics-of-mentors-in-tier-ones-mentees-coachees-need-to" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Understand the programme objectives/purpose and process
 Be self motivated
 Be able to articulate expectations and own objectives
 Meet commitments
 Accept feedback and act on it
 Listen
 Be self-aware</p>
<p>M.P. MUTUA
54</p>
<p>55</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mentees-coachees-need-to">Mentees/coachees need to...:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mentees-coachees-need-to" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Be receptive to and able to benefit from legitimate challenges
 Not to be a passive receiver but an active partner in the process
 To be ambitious with aspirations to go further
 To be realistically ambitious about their expectations of the programme
 Strong interpersonal skills</p>
<p>56
VOLUME 3</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mentees-coachees-need-to">Mentees/coachees need to:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mentees-coachees-need-to" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Prepared to take responsibility for their own actions
 Able to approach the relationship with respect, good humor and openness
 High belief in their ability to influence events in their favor
 Have the ability to reflect
 Be open
 Willing to engage in meaningful feedback
 Be trustworthy</p>
<p>Mentorship stages and methods (4)</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-c92d9f9a.jpeg" alt="img-46.jpeg"></p>
<p>58</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="phase-1-connection">Phase 1: Connection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#phase-1-connection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Rapport building
 Exploration of interests, motivations, needs, concerns &amp; expectations
 The mentor should have a personal devment discussion with the mentee which should broadly cover the following areas which help to establish the initial rship boundaries:</p>
<p>a. The mentees strengths, development interests &amp; areas needing enrichment
b. The specific skills the mentee will need to develop.
c. The development plan.
d. The roles and responsibilities of both parties.</p>
<p>59</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mentees-expectations-during-phase-i">Mentees' expectations during phase I<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mentees-expectations-during-phase-i" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Coaching: skills gap and uncertainty need to be addressed.
 Feedback: since they are there to learn and grow
 Role modelling: new to them.
 Acceptance &amp; Confirmation: they need to develop new skills
 Challenges: anxious of assignments &amp; other learning opportunities. Mentors will have to normalize these feelings and reassure them of success! So predict initial failure as a sign of courage, tenacity and a journey towards excellence!</p>
<p>60
English</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="phase-2-relationship-building-implementation">Phase 2: Relationship-building &amp; Implementation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#phase-2-relationship-building-implementation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Focuses on deepening the relationship
 There is increased interaction &amp; level of self-disclosure
 Definite shift on the continuum from dependence to interdependence
 Greater levels of commitment to the mentoring space through increased efforts and time being spent on the relationship and its core purpose.</p>
<p>61</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mentee-expectation-in-phase-ii">Mentee expectation in phase II<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mentee-expectation-in-phase-ii" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Guidance &amp; Support: normalizing fears and feelings and provide an accepting and safe space in which the mentee can be guided through these experiences.</p>
<p> Instructions: it helps reduce fears, anxieties and frustrations that could arise if this is not done correctly.</p>
<p> Feedback: communication and feedback that empowers the mentee to respond to reflections of growth, weaknesses and strengths</p>
<p> Encouragement: Speak to the mentee in the language of possibility, esp. when the mentees attempt to learn new skills</p>
<p>62</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="phase-iii-assessment">Phase III: Assessment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#phase-iii-assessment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Determines whether the objectives of the relationship have been met as well as the level of competence &amp; growth have been reached</p>
<p><strong>Critical questions in this phase:</strong></p>
<p> To what extent have the goals been met?
 Is the mentee competent?
 What have the mentors and mentees learnt?
 What unforeseen outcomes have occurred?
 How, if at all, has the mentorship journey affected the organization?
 What obstacles were encountered in the process?</p>
<p>63</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="step-iv-separation">Step IV: Separation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#step-iv-separation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Mentee requires less guidance from the mentor due to an increase in levels of confidence and competence
 Mentor play a less directive role in the mentees ability to make decisions
 Mentee initiates actions to further their growth &amp; devment
 Termination is evident and opportunities are leveraged to publicize achievements in the mentoring rships.
 Publicity is part of the feedback &amp; should be included in the organization's internal communication channels.
 Mentee motivates others who are yet to enter into the mentoring partnership.</p>
<p>64
M.P. MUTUA</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="there-can-be-challenges">There Can Be Challenges...<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#there-can-be-challenges" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Mentees can...</p>
<ul>
<li>Consume you</li>
<li>Be unfocused and not follow-through</li>
<li>Be manipulative</li>
<li>Be unwilling to commit to the relationship</li>
</ul>
<p>Mentors can...</p>
<ul>
<li>Burn out</li>
<li>Run into situations where issues really need professional help</li>
<li>Forget boundaries</li>
<li>Find themselves in odd situations (eg ethics, favors)</li>
</ul>
<p>65
M.P. MUTUA</p>

<p>DISCUSS THE DIFFERENCES BTN COACHING AND MENTORSHIP</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="b-coaching-for-community-health-services">B. COACHING FOR COMMUNITY HEALTH SERVICES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-coaching-for-community-health-services" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-fd4b146e.jpeg" alt="img-47.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-611e20a1.jpeg" alt="img-48.jpeg"></p>
<p>67</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> A leadership tool that is designed to help produce results
 A developmental approach to working and interacting with other people.
 Helps people develop their personal capabilities, interpersonal skills and capacity to understand and empathize with others
 Can help people understand more about their own challenges and make informed choices about their future
 Helps people strengthen their ability to use a range of influencing and leadership styles.
 Helps people feel more empowered to make a difference and improve their own effectiveness</p>
<p>68</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="definition">Definition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> the process whereby one individual helps another;</p>
<p>a. to unlock their natural ability;</p>
<p>b. to perform, learn and achieve;</p>
<p>c. to increase awareness of factors which determine performance;</p>
<p>d. to increase their sense of self responsibility and ownership of their performance;</p>
<p>e. to self-coach;</p>
<p>f. to identify and remove internal barriers to achievement. <em>MacLennan</em> (1999)</p>
<p>69</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="definition-continued">Definition Continued<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition-continued" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Coaching is the art of facilitating the performance, learning and development of another. Downey (2003)</p>
<p> Unlocking a persons potential to maximize their own performance. It is helping them to learn rather than teaching them. Whitmore (2003)</p>
<p> Ultimately coaching aims to bring out the best in an individual to enable the team to work better as a whole.</p>
<p>70
P. MUTUA</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="effective-supervisor-coaches-will">Effective supervisor "coaches" will...<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#effective-supervisor-coaches-will" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Establish a trusting relationship with all employees.
 Listen more than talk.
 Speak directly.
 Value and model continuous learning.
 Recognize their own limitations.
 Make an effort not to overuse strengths.
 Offer chances to take risks.
 Remain curious rather than defensive.
 Model accountability and ownership.
 Meet others where they are and help them move forward.
 Keep and optimistic attitude about people.</p>
<p>71
English</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="what-to-avoid-when-coaching">What to avoid when coaching...<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-to-avoid-when-coaching" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Giving solutions: The goal of coaching is to help the employee improve their own judgment and skill so that they can eventually succeed on their own. By jumping in with the solution, the coach does not support the employee to develop the ability to problem solve on their own.</p>
<p> Judging: giving verdict, jumping into conclusion, deciding ...</p>
<p> Assessing the employees performance</p>
<p> Blaming and criticizing from a supervisor undermines an employees perception that the supervisor is confident in their ability to solve the problem  can undermine the employees self-confidence.</p>
<p>72
English</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="types-of-coaching">Types of Coaching<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-coaching" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Personal/Life Coaching - A collaborative solution-focused, results-orientated and systematic process in which the coach facilitates the enhancement of work performance, life experience, self-directed learning and personal growth of the coachee. (counselling and encouraging clients through personal or career challenges)</p>
<p> Executive Coaching - Corporate/Business Coaching  focus on supporting an employee, either as an individual, as part of a team and/or organization to achieve improved business performance and operational effectiveness</p>
<p>73
400199491</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="types-of-coaching">Types of Coaching ...<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-coaching" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Specialty/Niche Coaching - expert in addressing one particular aspect of a person's life e.g. stress, career or rather a team of experts e.g., CHAs, CHOs, Doctors, Nurses etc
 Group Coaching - working with a number or individuals either to achieve a common goal within the group, or create an environment where individuals can co-coach each other.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="benefits-of-coaching">Benefits of coaching.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#benefits-of-coaching" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="to-the-coachee">...to the coachee<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#to-the-coachee" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p> A chance to discuss issues, blockages and/or concerns in your career development</p>
<p> Having someone (other than friends/colleagues/tutors) available to share difficult situations</p>
<p> Having someone to believe in you and your ability</p>
<p> Being given help to work out what it is you want from life and work</p>
<p> Being given help to develop a greater confidence</p>
<p> Learning to cope with the informal and formal structure of your future</p>
<p>76</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-benefits-for-the-coach">The benefits for the coach<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-benefits-for-the-coach" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> A chance to discover and work with colleagues/students from a different viewpoint
 An opportunity to share their knowledge, skills and experience
 The satisfaction of knowing that they have made a difference to someone else
 The huge amount of personal learning that can be taken from the experience
 The opportunity to create some reflective space in a hectic daily work schedule
 An increased skills base, credibility and reputation</p>
<p>77</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="steps-in-coaching-during-facilitative-supervision">Steps in coaching during facilitative supervision<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#steps-in-coaching-during-facilitative-supervision" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Stage One - Rapport Building Stage. Here the mentor/coach and mentee/coachee explore whether they can work together. Stage Two - Setting Direction Stage. coach and coachee clarify and refine what the relationship should achieve on both sides. Linking the medium to long term goals with what happens on a day to day basis is done.</p>
<p> Stage Three - Core Stage/ Progression. coach and coachee become more relaxed about challenging each other, exploring issues more deeply and experience mutual learning. coachee takes more of the lead in managing the relationship &amp; the process.</p>
<p>78</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="steps-in-coaching-during-facilitative-supervision">Steps in coaching during facilitative supervision<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#steps-in-coaching-during-facilitative-supervision" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Stage Four - Winding up. This occurs when the coachee has achieved a large part of their goals or feels equipped with the confidence, plans and insight to continue the journey under their own steam. Planning for a good ending is critical if both parties are to emerge from the process with a positive perception of the experience.</p>
<p> Stage Five Moving on. This stage is about reformulating the relationship, typically into a friendship in which both parties can meet each other on an ad hoc basis as a sounding board or a source of networking contacts. Individuals develop feelings of parting ways</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="definition">Definition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Refers to a face to face communication process in which one person tries to help another to understand a problem and identify a solution to that problem</p>
<p> It is the act of working with a client to help them clarify personal goals and find ways of overcoming their problems</p>
<p> <strong>Aim of counseling</strong>: to assist an individual to change behaviors that are interfering with normal life situations</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="principles-of-counselling">Principles of counselling<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-of-counselling" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Acceptance
 Individualization
 Privacy
 Confidentiality
 Accepting limitations
 Counseling is a process
 Counseling is for all
 Counselor doesn't deprive the right of self-choice but simply facilitates choice
 It is not advise giving
 It is not thinking for the client, but thinking with the client</p>
